< text>
Discovered this recently from an article online and decided to try it, mainly for the atmosphere. The environment is unique, a bit of an adventure getting to, and exactly what I hoped for. From the East Bay side, I took the last exit before the Carquinez bridge onto Stenmark drive, a two lane road which soon becomes one lane, requiring attention. The GPS advised that a portion of the road is unpaved, which is misleading: only the parking lot at the very end is packed dirt, close to the water.
The small marina has nice looking houseboats, and very interesting sculptures with clever lighting powered by small solar panels, which would make a night visit rather interesting if it were possible.
We got to Black Star Pirate BBQ early-ish, at 10:30 am on a Friday, half an hour before they opened. There already was a line of about ten people or so.
We tried four cuts of meat, and four sides, which came to about $95 before tip. Beef briskets (my favorite) rotisserie lamb (a new favorite), pulled chicken and pork. All of it served warm and with a light drizzle of BBQ sauce. The leftovers lasted us almost three days. The service is prompt and helpful and completely unpretentious.
Sitting at a table a little further out from the outdoor patio, we listened to chatter and water lapping at the rocks below. This is a calm atmosphere with caveats. I'd read reviews complaining of how loud the music was, and I can imagine that if they have live music, it could be. On the other hand, music can also be a good distraction from the popping sound of gunfire from the range over the hill. That sound, while not loud, might be unsettling to some. But it's not an ordinary place: out of the way, on the water, with nature and those odd art works, and people who care about their place, the quality of the food and customers. As said above, being this close to the water is a calming experience. The sounds from the range? Hey. It's Black Star Pirate BBQ, after all.
I would have loved this as a kid, and I loved remembering that. Of course, we'll go back. Early, on a weekday.</text>

Beautiful location and drive out there; felt secluded but really it's not far away. The establishment is so cute, service was very prompt and friendly (you order on arrival and they bring the food out super quick), and the food was so delicious! I will definitely be back!<//Text>

It sounded like an interesting story and a way to see a different part of the Bay area.

The experience was a great disappointment. The drive was OK, but the moment you get there you're charged $5 just to park your car in the dirt parking lot.It was a Saturday and the place seemed very busy. Disorganized might be another apt term.Once you had paid your bill, you had to find your own table, And since the COVID shutdowns are just starting to be relieved you still want to have some distance.

<review>3-27-21:
Atmosphere is great. Workers are very nice and friendly. The lady who took our order was very cool and offered her recommendations.

We must have come on an off day because the food was just so-so. Ordered the 2 meats and 3 side plate.

Tried the tri tip and the ribs. The tri tip was chewy, without much marbleization taste, and some pieces were surprisingly rare. The tri tip tasted like a lesser grade cut. Went here to buy a coffee with condensed milk (ca phe sua da) and had to wait for a long time to order. There was nothing comparable to a line, and when it was my turn to order, a rude guy cut in front of me to order. I would never give this place my business ever again. < review>
They charged me $30 rotate my tires, which, come to find out is a pretty astronomical price.  It took them about 6 minutes to switch the front with the rear and vice versa (which was awesome).  When I commented to the guy at the register at how high the price was if you looked at it as an hourly rate, he said well, if you tried to do it, it might take you half an hour to do each tire.  I didn't know people are now charging you for how long it would take you if you did the work yourself.  On top of that, I saw the price list they scan for labor.  The code they scanned clearly had the price as $9.99.  Since it was two tires, I could understand $20, but the guy manually changed it to $30.  Even at $20, that's a pretty high price to pay.  Do yourself a favor and go to Sports Chalet (literally a hundred yards away) and ask for David. He can rotate them for $5-$10.  Unfortunately, I found this out after I got swindled.
I assume this place is best for major problems or super expensive bikes/problems. Others should try searching elsewhere.<//review>

< rating>
4</rating>
<review>Performance Bike has a sale every week.  If the item you want isn't on sale that week, wait, it will likely go on sale in the next few weeks.  It is worth signing up for their online email lists.  They provide additional discounts (15%-20% off coupons on various items or for any purchase - including bikes).
This store, located in the Vons/Sport Chalet shopping center is one of the bigger stores.  The guys that work there (I say guys because I've never seen a woman working in this store) are very nice and generally helpful.  Most will give you the company line and if you press them, they will go off script and tell you what they personally think about items.
Prices for most stuff here is very competitive, but is hard to beat when on sale - which is nearly all the time.
If you buy accessories for your bike, they install them free.  If you need basic stuff, they will likely do it on the spot, and may or may not charge you depending on the complexity of the repair.
Very satisfied with Performance Bike in San Diego on Midway Drive.</review>< Date>
1256082900612</Date>

< Text>
Until this recent visit, I hadn't stepped foot in a cell phone store in probably 4 years.  My last upgrade was 2 and a half years ago, and I did it over the phone and had them ship it to me because I HATE the borderline harassing sales people that seem to inundate the staff in these places. Unfortunately I got overly excited when visiting the Polar Bears at the Zoo the other day, and launched my phone 20 feet across the exhibit, which resulted in a broken charging port and a cracked screen, so I had to bear (haha) down and make a trip into the Verizon store.

I will admit, I was expecting the worst.  It was a Saturday afternoon, and the parking lot was packed.  I thought for sure it would be an hour until I was even helped, and then I was going to have to fend off hundreds of  attempts to sell me stuff that I didn't want or need.  Boy was I wrong!

I was greeted when I walked into the store by a friendly associate who took my name and phone number and let me know that someone would  be with me within 5 minutes.  2 minutes later I was greeted by Naseer.  He asked me what I wanted to accomplish, and he focused on just that.  One of my main concerns was the price of a new phone, and how it would effect my bill because they had changed their upgrade process since the last time I had upgraded.  He sat me down, and explained everything clearly about my billing, and how it would change with a new phone.  Nothing sales, just genuinely there to help.  He then asked if I had a new phone in mind.  I told him about the 2 I had been researching, and he didn't try to sell me on either one.  He let me guide the conversation, asked me what I liked about my current phone, and used those attributes to compare to the two new phones I was interested in.  I decided on a phone, and I was out of there within 40 min of when I walked in the door.  I was shocked in the best way possible by Nasser's professionalism, and genuine caring attitude.</Text>

After canceling we were contacted by Sprint and offered 6gb of data and a $400 bill credit for the same phones for $104... Right. What would you do? Cancel? Yup.. Me too.

Less than 24 hours later we canceled our verizon service and returned the phones in brand new perfect condition.

verizon made zero attempts to retain our business before or after we cancelled with them.. But they were beyond happy to charge us a restocking fee of $124... Yup $124 fee for a product and service we were going to be overcharged for in the first place.

< review>
I am really pleased with the new management of this place. My only experience with the previous management was a large catering order that went horribly wrong - it arrived 2 hours late and with half the food missing. Luckily the bill was fixed to reflect that but since this was for our "welcome to our new office" party it was a huge disappointment and I had fully sworn the place off for anything in the future. Once I found out they were under new management, I decided to give them a whirl personally. The fish tacos are quite good and I do appreciate the option of mixing and matching which tacos I want to try. The build your own bowl is a cool option as well since I can personalize what I want. There aren't a ton of vegetarian options so personalizing is basically the only way to go. The food is kinda expensive for a normal work lunch so it's not someplace I go often. They offer Mexican coke in the bottle which I love and the staff is always very friendly and patient. The guacamole is absolutely one of the best I've ever had anywhere which will keep me coming back. :)</review>

<user>104345905733681135663</user><Name>Caitlyn Reinecker<//Name><Time>1505269269359< /Time>< rate>

< Text>
Un Mondo is a great contemporary twist on delicious Mexican food. The atmosphere is very clean and upbeat with a great system set up on how to order your food. How you order is you walk in and there's three big menus set up on the wall with cards below them to fill out on how exactly you want your food (just like Which Which). Then you take it to the person at the counter. And then take a seat and they will bring it to you in a jiffy.

The staff is Awesome as well. The owner is super friendly and informative. April who is at the counter is the best, super sweet and makes sure you are doing alright and you're happy with everything.

Lastly the food is bomb! Make sure to try all the salsas too :)</Text>

< Review>
I tried this place for the first time today and I loved it.  You build your own combo, which was a bit confusing, but the food is really fresh, healthy and tastes very good.  I very much liked the idea of having healthy food at a very reasonable price.  I ordered a bowl of steak meat with beans, lettuce, onion and corn, and it was only $10 including tax.  I will definitely come to this place again next time I visit San Diego area.<//Review>

< Review>
Good food. You can craft your own dishes (burritos, bowls, tacos) or you can pick one of their preplanned ones. You make your choices on paper and hand them to the cashier, who inputs it into their system. There are 6 or so meats; 15 or so additional ingredients like rice, cilantro, and sour cream; and a standard selection of salsas. Our meals came with chips. Food came out fast. There's parking in the lot right in front but it's often full.</Review>

<UserId.>109500349052667878251<//UserId.><user_name>Morgan Lai</user_name><date>1502304414749< /date><Rate>4</Rate>< Text>
It's a nice California-style taco place, I came by for their Taco Tuesday.

They don't advertise it at all as far as I can see, but they offered carnitas tacos and pastor tacos, both for $1.50 each on Taco Tuesday.

Maybe it's because I went in late-ish at 8:30pm, but they are the slowest taco place I have ever been to before. There weren't too many people in there, maybe half the seats were empty, but they took 15-20 minutes to prepare each order.

Also, looking around, everyone's orders were rife with errors. For-here orders became to-go. My order sat around for a while because the cashier assumed I left for some reason until I asked. Some people got flags to put on their tables with their order numbers and some didn't. Pretty strange.

The pastor was unusual - it was literally just the pastor meat sitting on tortilla. However, they crisped up the meat really nicely, so it tasted good, particularly with the orange salsa, so I'm not sure I can complain. However, I wonder if that's how it was meant to come out or if they messed it up. I've never seen a bare taco like that before not at a place where you can add in fillings yourself.

The carnitas was also nicely crisped up. I think they messed up my order the first time around - I asked for 2 regular and 1 without cilantro, and all 3 came out with just bare meat and onions. I went back and ordered another and this time it was with onions and cilantro. I'm a little unclear whether the first one was the mistake, or the second one, but I assume with the cilantro is the way it was supposed to come. I like the flavor of the pastor better, but I preferred this one for having the accompaniments of onions and cilantro.

The food was good, and at a great price on Taco Tuesday, but it was a pretty weird experience how they seemed to screw up practically everything that could be screwed up.< /Text>

Went to ER with intense pain in my back near the shoulder blade area to under arm into upper front of chest. The pain had been present for at least a week and was not effected by physical or emotional stress.
Upon being brought back to visit ER DR I was given an EKG. The DR came in and asked a number of questions regarding my heart and family history of heart issues. Told him I had never had cardio issues but my farther pass at age 59 with a heart attack. I told the DR I had just completed a full cardio work up within the last few weeks. He asked exactly what did that mean because a cardio work up means different thinks. He asked if the work up had included an ultra sound, which I responded yes. I then asked him to listen to what I had to say about a stem cell injection procedure I had back in August which did not go well. He seemed reluctant to listen to what I was saying and kept his eyes downward as I explained what had happened. He then applied pressure to the top of my head and asked me to turn my head. When I turned my head to the left it cause the pain to increase. The DR then said I should make an appointment with my GP to have that addressed. DR said the ER was not there to address the issue relating to pain associated with my neck.  He then ordered a frontal chest X-ray and blood work. After he left the room a nurse (assuming she was a nurse could have been another DR) gave me 4 baby aspirin to take. It is also worth mentioning the DR asked me twice if I had ever had an angiogram. Which I had not. At this point it was obvious the DR had me on a heart attack protocol. which surprised me since my EKG and blood pressure were within the normal range.
After the X-ray and blood test I was sent back to the waiting room to wait for test results. The longer I sat there the more I realized my back pain was not going to be addressed. I was also very concerned the focus was on a heart condition and not what I was there to have address.
I believe the DR had a predetermined notion I was in some type of heart related stress and nothing was going to change his mind.
